  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_103f28cc-f34c-4f81-9519-198be45b2911'
      });
    }

  <span id="freeText16225263778980194112" style="display:none">Callie Hayes is living a life of fear and disillusionment when she volunteers for a psychology experiment that promises to turn her life around. As her orientation proceeds, Callie becomes frightened by the secrecy and evasion she encounters. When she demands to be released from the program, she is suddenly dropped into a terrifying alien world and into a perilous battle between good and evil. With limited resources and only a few cryptic words to guide her, Callie embarks on a life-changing journey. Will she decipher the plans the Benefactor has established for her escape, or will she succumb to the deception of the Arena?</span>

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/434791-i-can-t-seem-to-get-to-finish-this-book">I Can&#39;t seem to get to finish this book , It has been almost 2 weeks since I started it (maybe more) , and man I didn&#39;t rich 100 pages , I don&#39;t feel it . Am I missing something here ? Would it get any better ? tell me it is going to get better , anything that would make me want to continue reading this ..</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_434791'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F142023.Arena">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/434791-i-can-t-seem-to-get-to-finish-this-book">5 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/434791-i-can-t-seem-to-get-to-finish-this-book">See all 2 answers</a>
</li>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/91228305-cathy-jones"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/91228305-cathy-jones">Cathy Jones</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I had the same experience. The lack of character development made me not care about the main character one way or another for the first several chapte<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I had the same experience. The lack of character development made me not care about the main character one way or another for the first several chapters. It seemed just too contrived. <br /><br />However, I always finish a book once I start it, always hoping it will get better. And this one did get better as it went along. I am glad I finished it, although I can’t say it’s the best book I’ve ever read. Some parts of it just didn’t make sense to me. And some scenes seem repetitive. But it is an entertaining read as you go further along, and the point the author is trying to make about faith is a good one. In my opinion, it’s worth finishing, although I can’t say I’d put it on my list to recommend to others. <br /><a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_69381235" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/69381235" />
    <a title="Dina Sleiman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2643813-dina-sleiman"><img alt="Dina Sleiman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1414159927p2/2643813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/69381235?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dina Sleiman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dina Sleiman" href="/user/show/2643813-dina-sleiman">Dina Sleiman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Dina by: </span>
      Christi Sleiman
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2643813-dina-sleiman?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer69381235" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4880112435957384162">I wish I could give this book a sixth star. Take a dash of Pilgrim’s Progress, toss in a good helping of The Matrix, and you get Arena by Karen Hancock. Talk about a book I couldn’t put down. My teenaged daughter highly recommended Arena to me, and it turned out to be one of the most fascinating and unique novels I have ever read. Sci-fi fans will go especially crazy for this book, but everyone will appreciate the finely crafted allegory of the Christian experience. <br/><br/>Callie Hayes thinks she is si</span>
  <span id="freeText4880112435957384162" style="display:none">I wish I could give this book a sixth star. Take a dash of Pilgrim’s Progress, toss in a good helping of The Matrix, and you get Arena by Karen Hancock. Talk about a book I couldn’t put down. My teenaged daughter highly recommended Arena to me, and it turned out to be one of the most fascinating and unique novels I have ever read. Sci-fi fans will go especially crazy for this book, but everyone will appreciate the finely crafted allegory of the Christian experience. <br /><br />Callie Hayes thinks she is signing up for a psychology experiment, but finds herself whisked away to…well, she isn’t quite sure. Is it a holographic fantasy, an alien world, or an alternate reality? All she knows for sure is that she, like everyone else lost in this strange place, is desperate to get back home safely. Along the way she will meet a host of strange creatures, incredible challenges, and bizarre mysteries. <br /><br />This book offers more than just adventure, however. Callie forges many deep relationships with the other victims of this experiment, and learns much about her own desires, about life, and about what is truly important. She also discovers a unique connection with a special man, but can it survive the Arena?<br /><br />The Arena serves as a backdrop for some of life’s most pressing questions and realities. As Callie and her friends move through different levels and phases of this unusual realm, the relationship to our own spiritual growth and development becomes clear. <br /><br />I particularly liked the concept of “the link,” a way to touch and communicate with “Elhanu” who served as God within the story. The armor given to those who passed through “the Gate” was quickly deactivated by fear and could only be reactivated by reaching within and finding “the link” again. This is so true in our own lives. The parallels to spiritual warfare in this book were exquisite, and clearly demonstrated the power and responsibility of the Christian believer in battling and gaining victory over the enemy. No less stunning was Hancock’s presentation of how one must first come to God and salvation and the varying struggles people go through in order to find Him. The powerful spiritual messages in this book are too many to enumerate in one review.<br /><br />If you read one Christian novel this year, let me recommend Arena. No matter where you are in your walk with God, you will find something within its pages that will minister to you, enlighten you, and draw you closer to Him.<br /><br />Review by Dina L. Sleiman<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13247128823590629859">To the person who recommended this book to me, first of all, I would like to say, "Mother, that was one weird bus stop!" <br/><br/>What do you get when you combine a western novel with a sci-fi and a romance and <i>Pilgrim's Progress</i>? You get a cowboy shooting blue laser light at demons to save his true love. That's what.   <span id="freeText13247128823590629859" style="display:none">To the person who recommended this book to me, first of all, I would like to say, "Mother, that was one weird bus stop!" <br /><br />What do you get when you combine a western novel with a sci-fi and a romance and <i>Pilgrim's Progress</i>? You get a cowboy shooting blue laser light at demons to save his true love. That's what. And then you stay up late into the night trying to find out what happens, and you come away with the same sort of impression you have after eating sushi or kimchee for the first time--weird, but strangely good and even inspiring.<br /><br />I totally agreed with the message the author was trying to convey, and I thought it was a good reminder. There were some plot holes and redundant battles, but overall, the story was intriguing and insightful at the same time. And definitely different.<br /><br />The only thing that really bothered me, and this is trivial, was the characters' diets: hot dogs, eggs, bacon, and once before going into battle, macaroni and cheese with a slab of beef. GROSS! If the enemy don't getcha, your diet will!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_954651616" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/954651616" />
    <a title="E. Melure" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31903159-e-melure"><img alt="E. Melure" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/954651616?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="E. Melure" class="user" itemprop="url" name="E. Melure" href="/user/show/31903159-e-melure">E. Melure</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31903159-e-melure?shelf=christian-fantasy">christian-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer954651616" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17285106126537742111">I typically have a hard time with Christian Fiction, because, to agree with a few of the reviews, that genre tends to be too "in-your-face" or too "Christian-cliché." I happen to be someone who knows God to be much more than cute quotes and easy street, so I get slightly repulsed by those types of books because they do not accurately portray the difficulty of life -- with and without God.<br/><br/>While granting my limited knowledge of this category, I found Arena to be an incredible example of the walk o</span>
  <span id="freeText17285106126537742111" style="display:none">I typically have a hard time with Christian Fiction, because, to agree with a few of the reviews, that genre tends to be too "in-your-face" or too "Christian-cliché." I happen to be someone who knows God to be much more than cute quotes and easy street, so I get slightly repulsed by those types of books because they do not accurately portray the difficulty of life -- with and without God.<br /><br />While granting my limited knowledge of this category, I found Arena to be an incredible example of the walk of a Christian. No two Christians have the same testimony as to how they found God, and this book introduces a lot of different angles (while focusing on Callie's story of course). Also granted, is that no book is perfect or will be able to cover all of the intricacies included in finding and following God, so of course this book can not cover them all either.<br /><br />Where a lot of Hancock's allegory can be seen as "obvious" to those comfortable in the genre and the Christian walk in general, others may be able to glean new insight from her presentation. She begins where all begin: dropped into a world unknown unsure as to what the next step is. Each character will either find their way to the "God" representative character, or they won't. Hancock intertwines the problems we fact today in easy to relate to situations, effectively showing how different people will react differently. Temptation, fear, anger, lust, depression, all of these (and more) topics we face today -- Christians and non-Christians alike -- are all introduced to Callie or Pierce, oftentimes with a contrasting minor character who handles a similar situation differently. <br /><br />Each section of the book promotes the characters to the next level of their journey (or faith, to follow the allegory). Some characters make it, some don't, which also is seen in today's world with Christianity. The characters must mature in their understanding and abilities as they fight to reach truth and return home, and it was creative and enrapturing to me how Hancock was able to convey the relevance to people today. <br /><br />I recommend this book to all because Christians and non-Christians alike do, and will, face the same emotional and spiritual torments these characters go through, and only our choices and reactions will determine where we go next. However, I do recommend reading it with full knowledge of the sub-novel story being one of the Christian walk. Approaching it this way may help avoid being broadsided when it pops out. It is Christian fiction after all.<br /><br />I read this first about 6 or so years ago and it still remains my favorite Christian fiction.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17285106126537742111" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_839603799" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <span id="freeText17094315115714460478" style="display:none"><b><i>Arena</i> by Karen Hancock<br />.1/5 Stars</b><br /><br /><br />I like to start my reviews with the best parts, themes, characters or whatever I think makes the book standout. This book has already been a heavy discussion piece in my "book club." However, not for the reasons a book should be. The only things about this book that I can muster in a positive aspect are the following: the message and the overall idea.<br /><br />Unfortunately, the execution of the idea was atrocious. The writing was bland, repetitive and overall boring. There is virtually no character development. Of the few characters that were developed, they would go through a personality change instantly, remain that way for a few pages then revert back or change all together again. There were a few phrases that were used multiple times over. <br /><br />Most of all, the story never meshed together. To me, it was just bad story telling. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45413513" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13080178777745353582">Callie Hayes grudgingly agrees to participate in a psychology study as moral support for a friend. However, frightened by the examiners' secrecy and evasiveness (one vanishes before her eyes), she tries to escape but finds herself cast into the Arena, a testing ground for participants of the study. Armed with only a guidebook and minimal supplies, she is soon forced to trust the enigmatic Pierce, a man who claims to have spent the past five years in the Arena. As Callie journeys toward the Gate,</span>
  <span id="freeText13080178777745353582" style="display:none">Callie Hayes grudgingly agrees to participate in a psychology study as moral support for a friend. However, frightened by the examiners' secrecy and evasiveness (one vanishes before her eyes), she tries to escape but finds herself cast into the Arena, a testing ground for participants of the study. Armed with only a guidebook and minimal supplies, she is soon forced to trust the enigmatic Pierce, a man who claims to have spent the past five years in the Arena. As Callie journeys toward the Gate, supposedly her ticket out, she learns more about the mysterious Benefactor conducting the test and uses her developing faith in him to find the way home. However, this path is laid with false trails, traps, and false messiahs eager to destroy Callie and the friends she makes along the way. Hancock's first novel is an allegorical blend of fantasy and sf depicting the tests a soul faces that strengthen or destroy belief in God. Hints of the post-apocalyptic world of Mad Max surface, along with the sense of climbing through the wardrobe into C.S. Lewis's allegorical Narnia. A classic in the making for the modern era, with appeal for fans of Lewis and Kathy Tyers ("Firebird Trilogy"), this is required for all collections.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7853886026628685027">I enjoyed this book and didn't find that it was preachy in the Christian sense, despite the fact that is is listed as inspirational fiction. I can certainly see the parallels and allegory, but I do not believe that it would be a turn off to someone who was not a deeply religious person. I thought the message transcended Christianity as a moral tale of life, asserting ourselves and the choices we make. I enjoyed the little bit of an added happy ending as well. Sucker for the guy getting the girl.</span>

<div id="review_626396388" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/626396388" />
    <a title="Kibbenza" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8861987-kibbenza"><img alt="Kibbenza" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340562576p2/8861987.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/626396388?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kibbenza" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kibbenza" href="/user/show/8861987-kibbenza">Kibbenza</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer626396388" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer180735431008654837">I'm kind of torn with this book. On the one hand, I did kind of enjoy it. The writing wasn't anything spectacular, and the story was kind of strange, but it was interesting in a way that kept me reading (although more slowly than I would with a book that really captured me).<br/><br/>Callie, at first, is a bit of a boring character. She seemed pretty stuffy for someone that young. I can understand serious, or reserved, but she came across as way older than she was supposed to be. So, it was kind of hard t</span>
  <span id="freeText180735431008654837" style="display:none">I'm kind of torn with this book. On the one hand, I did kind of enjoy it. The writing wasn't anything spectacular, and the story was kind of strange, but it was interesting in a way that kept me reading (although more slowly than I would with a book that really captured me).<br /><br />Callie, at first, is a bit of a boring character. She seemed pretty stuffy for someone that young. I can understand serious, or reserved, but she came across as way older than she was supposed to be. So, it was kind of hard to relate to her at first. I was easily interested in her journey though, once it got into the Arena world itself. Sometimes I felt she spent too much time thinking. It seems like a bad idea to get that lost in thought when the environment is as hostile as hers was! She changed a great deal throughout the book, which was fun to see.<br /><br />At any rate, I did get somewhat invested in the story, which got better. I really did enjoy that, though there was romance, that wasn't the whole focus of the book. It was there, but the book was full of much more than that. <br /><br />I think the thing that really didn't go over well with me was the God/faith allegory. It felt too forced and overly obvious, and it just... didn't really belong. It went from a sci-fi type feeling to "this is an overt metaphor for God, have faith and all things are possible". Which is fine, but doesn't really fit with what the story was shaping up to be. It was a strange shift, and I felt like the rest of the book focused too much, and gave too much credit to that. It kind of overshadowed what the characters were going through and accomplishing. <br /><br />I guess my biggest complaint aside from the overt allegory was that the book changed pace and tone so much. Things were skimmed over, which I felt took away from how awful the Arena was supposed to be. And then it went from terrible, to a luxury resort, to terrible again. That kind of back and forth was strange! <br /><br />So... yeah, I'm just really torn with this one.<br /><br />I guess all I can say is that I didn't hate it, and I don't regret reading it. Which isn't the best compliment you can give a book... <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="180735431008654837" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_12032778" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/12032778" />
    <a title="Joeschmoe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/760110-joeschmoe"><img alt="Joeschmoe" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/12032778?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joeschmoe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joeschmoe" href="/user/show/760110-joeschmoe">Joeschmoe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer12032778" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15279084284299739372">I'm not sure where to start. Though I enjoy this book from a purely sci-fi standpoint, its undertone is simply unbearable. Every time I manage to forget the fact that this book was written as a (rather shitty) allegory, something will come up that practically flaunts it. The best way to put it is your friend is telling a mildly amusing story. He means it to be humorous, but you find it interesting nonetheless. Yet every time you manage to forget how stupid the point of your friend's story is, he</span>
  <span id="freeText15279084284299739372" style="display:none">I'm not sure where to start. Though I enjoy this book from a purely sci-fi standpoint, its undertone is simply unbearable. Every time I manage to forget the fact that this book was written as a (rather shitty) allegory, something will come up that practically flaunts it. The best way to put it is your friend is telling a mildly amusing story. He means it to be humorous, but you find it interesting nonetheless. Yet every time you manage to forget how stupid the point of your friend's story is, he'll over emphasize a terrible pun, nudge you painfully in the ribs and wink profusely (and not even the good subtle winking, the kind of winking where the whole damn side of his face scrunches up and his other eye squints).<br /><br />Don't even get me started on the main character. Stupid and blind to the point of making me seriously wonder if she was an allegory for the mentally handicapped, whoseit (I don't even remember her name, and it was only a few weeks ago that I stopped caring about this book) embodied poorly written main characters everywhere. This woman's conceit eclipses the average galaxy in size and mass. I would rather violate myself with a rake than deal with another page of this vapid crap.<br /><br />And yet, the 'allegory' story is extremely interesting, enough so to brutally force me to raise my rating from an impossible negative three, to a two star rating. If the author would focus on actually writing sci-fi than writing pointless crap that's been done to death, she might actually produce a tolerable book.<br /><br />I suppose I'll go get that rake now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15279084284299739372" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer150928314" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer6648941333107127448">I can't believe I've waited this long to read this novel. Couldn't put it down. If you enjoy Kathy Tyers, you'll like this one. A few descriptions are a tad bit sensual, but they are written with taste and make sense within the context of the story. I do agree with some of the reviewers that at times the allegory was a little obvious, but hey... so was the allegory in The Chronicles of Narnia and I loved that. It really does make you look at your Christian walk in a new light. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4237611249502447257">A friend recommended this to me, so I sat down and read it -- in about six hours. I sometimes found myself skim-reading, and the pacing in the second half was rather slow. But I liked the symbolism and she had some great and unique touches here and there. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer349283960" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7890256046439721513">A very unique book, speculative in nature. When Meg and Callie sign up for an experiment at the Univ. of Arizona they have no idea where it will take them. They separately end up in a place called the "Arena", on another world and are confronted with life and death struggles in dealing with the environment.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2347422957" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2347422957" />
    <a title="Michaela Selway" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/80169322-michaela-selway"><img alt="Michaela Selway" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522883162p2/80169322.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2347422957?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michaela Selway" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michaela Selway" href="/user/show/80169322-michaela-selway">Michaela Selway</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2347422957" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5116431470637036098">What a book. I literally have no other words for it. I have read this book about 5 times and never fail to see something new.<br/><br/>I'm just writing a brief overview as I HATE reading reviews and seeing accidental spoilers :D hope it helps to give a crazy short overview :)<br/><br/>So it opens with Callie and her best friend, Meg, signing up for some experiment that is supposed to change their lives. The only problem is that Callie is SUPER dubious because this is not the first experiment Meg has dragged her too</span>
  <span id="freeText5116431470637036098" style="display:none">What a book. I literally have no other words for it. I have read this book about 5 times and never fail to see something new.<br /><br />I'm just writing a brief overview as I HATE reading reviews and seeing accidental spoilers :D hope it helps to give a crazy short overview :)<br /><br />So it opens with Callie and her best friend, Meg, signing up for some experiment that is supposed to change their lives. The only problem is that Callie is SUPER dubious because this is not the first experiment Meg has dragged her too, and this one is solely because Meg is interested in the guy. How many times have we all been in a situation like this?? In this situation I didn't know who I related too actually. Callie, the ever-questioning critic, or Meg, the one who blindly follows. I guess both. Whoops :P<br /><br />Long story short, Callie doesn't end up listening to the instructions of the game as she ends up being freaked out by some weird dude sitting in reception. Now that sounds like me!! She gets thrown into this 'other' world and for the first however long, instead of taking in her surroundings and figuring out where she is, she tries to figure out what happened in a literal sense. Did they teleport her? Is she drugged? We can already see from the get-go that our gal is taking the path of MOST resistance.<br /><br />As she begins to make her way through this strange world with strange creatures, Callie takes on a motto that she has carried for most of her life: you can't trust anyone. Though this may not seem apparent at the beginning, Callie has had serious family problems and whether she tries to or not, she can't trust anyone for fear that they will leave her, disappoint her or hurt her. Not only this but she is also plagued with her childhood fear that never left her.<br /><br />As always, the mighty man - or in this case super cynical grumpy man - enters the scene and tries to at least warn Callie about the dangers she is about to face. Of course, knowing what we now know about her, Callie doesn't listen and ends up putting herself in harms way, only to be saved by this mysterious man - Pierce. <br /><br />This is where the God figure enters in. Elhanu. I cannot even try to pronounce this name out loud as everyone I know says it differently. But he comes to be a character that you begin to love and trust, even though you yourself aren't the one living out this crazy existence. Elhanu provides a guide, and a connection to himself. He says that he will go forth with these people to protect them, that if they only trust in him, he will show them the way.<br /><br />Until this point in the book I had not seen any Christian references. And I think that is the beauty of Karen's writing. It is so captivating, it draws you in with the disappointment, the heartbreak, the tension and the joy when they succeed at a challenge. And it shows you God, reveals Him to you in a new way that I had never encountered before. In this book, God is portrayed as a friend that the group meet along the way and it isn't until later that they find out who Elhanu was all along. He was a companion, a brother, a father, and a guide. Someone who knew what you were thinking but were too afraid to admit. Who knew the depths of your heart and still loved you. He gave soft encouragement where needed, but knew when to just sit beside you and comfort you.<br /><br />The rest of this book centres around this idea. As Pierce and Callie face their fears, they learn to turn it over to God.<br /><br />If you want to go read the rest of my review click the following link:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://michaelajaneruth.wixsite.com/a-thousand-lives/blog/arena-karen-hancock">https://michaelajaneruth.wixsite.com/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5116431470637036098" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3597518475" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3597518475" />
    <a title="K L" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77289651-k-l"><img alt="K L" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521522587p2/77289651.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3597518475?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K L" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K L" href="/user/show/77289651-k-l">K L</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3597518475" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10604196637664122810">After reading and enjoying Karen Hanock's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4532622.The_Enclave' title='The Enclave by Karen Hancock' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Enclave</a>, I picked up this title. It wasn't what I expected. <br/><br/>Sometimes it felt as though the story was only dipping toes in the water instead of jumping in. The character development was minimal on the main character, Callie's, part. Pierce was better described but mostly only about a traumatic past. Meg never changed. There was much more in interactions between characters, the world around them, ect. that could've been fleshed out. A few examples: <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(v</a></span>
  <span id="freeText10604196637664122810" style="display:none">After reading and enjoying Karen Hanock's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4532622.The_Enclave" title="The Enclave by Karen Hancock" rel="nofollow noopener">The Enclave</a>, I picked up this title. It wasn't what I expected. <br /><br />Sometimes it felt as though the story was only dipping toes in the water instead of jumping in. The character development was minimal on the main character, Callie's, part. Pierce was better described but mostly only about a traumatic past. Meg never changed. There was much more in interactions between characters, the world around them, ect. that could've been fleshed out. A few examples: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Wendell followed a false messiah for years, and I thought we'd hear his distress at discovering this but we don't. It's skipped over. It would've been interesting, too, to see more of Mander the false benefactor. He was evil, no doubt, but his portrayal could've been more convincingly so. Another thing: after passing through the gate, the author skips ahead; suddenly Callie no longer has problems climbing, and Pierce is a leader. We get a summary, essentially, but don't get to see them change ourselves.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />My main frustration was from about 40 percent on, the plot lost a lot of momentum. There was little for the characters to do. The plot later picks up again, then slows down. The problem being everything is absolute hell (fighting, capture, even torture) and when a safe haven is reached, it's easy street. Vacillating between extremes messed up the flow of the novel. <br /><br />I stuck it out and finished the entire book. The ending was worth reading, but I could've skipped several chapters to get to it and been happy.<br /><br />The idea is very creative, but for those reasons, I could only rate it three starts.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10604196637664122810" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2530924984" />
    <a title="Lara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24337665-lara"><img alt="Lara" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2530924984?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lara" href="/user/show/24337665-lara">Lara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/30372202-arena">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24337665-lara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2530924984" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2445605140796252301">A Christian allegory, which I knew going in, so I should not have been surprised when the infodump halfway through about the noble ruler and the rebellious prince and the internal bond between the noble ruler and those who have faith in him was dropped with a resounding *thump*. Also full of just <i>adorable</i> little nuggets about how sexual desires are fleeting and deceptive (also, the two women who seek out sex and are stated to be sexually attractive get raped and one of them turns evil), sex drea</span>
  <span id="freeText2445605140796252301" style="display:none">A Christian allegory, which I knew going in, so I should not have been surprised when the infodump halfway through about the noble ruler and the rebellious prince and the internal bond between the noble ruler and those who have faith in him was dropped with a resounding *thump*. Also full of just <i>adorable</i> little nuggets about how sexual desires are fleeting and deceptive (also, the two women who seek out sex and are stated to be sexually attractive get raped and one of them turns evil), sex dreams are the tool of the bad guys and you should pray before you go to bed, true love waits even if true love will forget all about you once you're out of this allegory and back in the real world, and doubting God-Equivalent's master plan even for a second means you deserve every bad thing that might happen to you due to that moment of doubt.<br /><br />*sigh* There's a reason I don't read inspirational fiction any more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2445605140796252301" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2410506035" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2410506035" />
    <a title="Amy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68316833-amy"><img alt="Amy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529820062p2/68316833.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2410506035?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/68316833-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2410506035" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4912733343972584576">Too many adjectives. This book was overly defined, written poorly, and not very interesting in my opinion. In multiple instances, a chapter would begin in the middle of a battle, when at the end of the last chapter we were sitting in a safe house. What's worse, the author wouldn't flashback or explain, plus she would randomly start using new terms that were impossible to understand. There was an unsatisfying ending, but it could have been worse. The main characters were underdeveloped, or develo</span>
  <span id="freeText4912733343972584576" style="display:none">Too many adjectives. This book was overly defined, written poorly, and not very interesting in my opinion. In multiple instances, a chapter would begin in the middle of a battle, when at the end of the last chapter we were sitting in a safe house. What's worse, the author wouldn't flashback or explain, plus she would randomly start using new terms that were impossible to understand. There was an unsatisfying ending, but it could have been worse. The main characters were underdeveloped, or developed in a very direct and boring manner. The relationships were okay, but the wording used felt forced or unnatural. I'm no expert whatsoever, but I can identify basic writing qualities, and this book was definitely lacking in originality. If you are only interesting in a basic story with mediocre characters, then the book will suffice.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4912733343972584576" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bzHf+2ez1avpLHHPHF4RLH+yeDdgJZj0VR03efN0lAc3gghFptWquluyRf7BpoJMuSmdXAOXzCv80AWvyYKyNg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Ky565FRtdf1h4jOrB3gXX1/SPzy7tb+mcNvcTcuz20Vzna1alQsK7NN8B5ragIQ/mUnaV9gH63nZFu6b8UX9dA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
